<li><a href="/wiki/Haklau_Min" title="Haklau Min">Haklau Min / Hailufeng / Hai Lok Hong</a> (<span lang="zh">海陸豐話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Hái-Lo̍k-hong-ōa</span></i>)* (Transitionary with <a href="/wiki/Teo-Swa_Min" class="mw-redirect" title="Teo-Swa Min">Teo-Swa Min</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hailu_dialect" title="Hailu dialect">Hoiluk</a> <a href="/wiki/Hakka_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hakka language">Hakka</a>)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Haifeng_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Haifeng dialect">Haifeng dialect</a> (<span lang="zh">海豐話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Hái-hong-ōa</span></i>)*</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haifeng_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Haifeng dialect">Lufeng dialect</a> (<span lang="zh">陸豐話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Lo̍k-hong-ōa</span></i>)*</li></ul></li>
<li>Northern <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Straits" class="mw-redirect" title="Malacca Straits">Malacca Straits</a> Hokkien
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Penang_Hokkien" title="Penang Hokkien">Penang Hokkien</a> (<span lang="zh">檳城福建話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Peng-siâⁿ Hok-kiàn-ōa / Pin-siâⁿ Hok-kiàn-ōa</span></i>／<span lang="zh">庇能福建話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Pī-néeng Hok-kiàn-ōa</span></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medan_Hokkien" title="Medan Hokkien">Medan Hokkien</a> (<span lang="zh">棉蘭福建話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Mî-lân Hok-kiàn-oā</span></i>)</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Longyan_dialect" title="Longyan dialect">Longyan dialect</a> (<span lang="zh">龍巖腔</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Liông-nâ khioⁿ</span></i>)* (Transitionary with <a href="/wiki/Changting_dialect" title="Changting dialect">Changting</a> <a href="/wiki/Hakka_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hakka language">Hakka</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwanese Hokkien</a> (<span lang="zh">台語</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Tâi-gí / Tâi-gú</span></i>／<span lang="zh">臺灣話</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Tâi-oân-ōe</span></i>／<span lang="zh">臺灣閩南語</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Tâi-oân Bân-lâm-gú / Tâi-oân Bân-lâm-gí</span></i>)*
<ul><li>Various dialects per region descended variously and mixed from the above as well (See <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien#Quanzhou–Zhangzhou_inclinations" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwanese Hokkien#Quanzhou–Zhangzhou inclinations</a>)</li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>
</div>
<p>*<a href="/wiki/Haklau_Min" title="Haklau Min">Haklau Min</a> (<i>Hai Lok Hong</i>, including the Haifeng and Lufeng dialect), Chaw'an / Zhao'an (詔安話), <a href="/wiki/Longyan_Min" class="mw-redirect" title="Longyan Min">Longyan Min</a>, and controversially, <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwanese</a>, are sometimes considered as not Hokkien anymore, besides being under <a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a> (Min Nan). On the other hand, those under <a href="/wiki/Longyan_Min" class="mw-redirect" title="Longyan Min">Longyan Min</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaoshan_Min" title="Chaoshan Min">Teo-Swa Min</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhenan_Min" title="Zhenan Min">Zhenan Min</a> have some to little mutual intelligibility with Hokkien, while <a href="/wiki/Datian_Min" title="Datian Min">Datian Min</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Min" title="Zhongshan Min">Zhongshan Min</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hainanese" title="Hainanese">Qiong</a>-<a href="/wiki/Leizhou_Min" title="Leizhou Min">Lei Min</a> also have historical linguistic roots with Hokkien, but are significantly divergent from it in terms of phonology and vocabulary, and thus have almost little to no mutual intelligibility with Hokkien.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison">Comparison</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Comparison"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Amoy_dialect" title="Amoy dialect">Amoy dialect</a> (Xiamen) is a variant of the Tung'an dialect. Majority of <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwanese</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Tainan" title="Tainan">Tainan</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Taichung" title="Taichung">Taichung</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a>, is also heavily based on Tung'an dialect while incorporating some vowels of Zhangzhou dialect, whereas <a href="/wiki/Southern_Peninsular_Malaysian_Hokkien" title="Southern Peninsular Malaysian Hokkien">Southern Peninsular Malaysian Hokkien</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_Hokkien" title="Singaporean Hokkien">Singaporean Hokkien</a>, is based on the Tung'an dialect, with <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Hokkien" title="Philippine Hokkien">Philippine Hokkien</a> on the Quanzhou dialect, and <a href="/wiki/Penang_Hokkien" title="Penang Hokkien">Penang Hokkien</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Medan_Hokkien" title="Medan Hokkien">Medan Hokkien</a> on the Zhangzhou dialect. There are some variations in pronunciation and vocabulary between Quanzhou and Zhangzhou dialects. The grammar is generally the same.
</p><p>Additionally, extensive contact with the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese language</a> has left a legacy of Japanese loanwords in Taiwanese Hokkien. On the other hand, the variants spoken in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> have a substantial number of loanwords from <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> and to a lesser extent, from <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and other Chinese varieties, such as the closely related Teochew and some <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>. Meanwhile, in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, there are also a few <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Spanish" title="Philippine Spanish">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>) loanwords, while it is also currently a norm to frequently <a href="/wiki/Codeswitch" class="mw-redirect" title="Codeswitch">codeswitch</a> with <a href="/wiki/Philippine_English" title="Philippine English">English</a>, Tagalog, and in some cases other <a href="/wiki/Philippine_languages" title="Philippine languages">Philippine languages</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Cebuano_language" title="Cebuano language">Cebuano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiligaynon_language" title="Hiligaynon language">Hiligaynon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Bikol" title="Central Bikol">Bicol Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilocano_language" title="Ilocano language">Ilocano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chavacano" title="Chavacano">Chavacano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waray_language" title="Waray language">Waray-waray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kapampangan_language" title="Kapampangan language">Kapampangan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pangasinan_language" title="Pangasinan language">Pangasinense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sorsogon_language" title="Northern Sorsogon language">Northern Sorsogonon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Sorsogon_language" title="Southern Sorsogon language">Southern Sorsogonon</a>, etc.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mutual_intelligibility">Mutual intelligibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Mutual intelligibility"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tong'an, Xiamen, Taiwanese, Singaporean dialects as a group are more <a href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually intelligible">mutually intelligible</a>, but it is less so amongst the forementioned group, Quanzhou dialect, and Zhangzhou dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the Min Nan varieties of Teochew and Amoy are 84% phonetically similar including the pronunciations of un-used Chinese characters as well as same characters used for different meanings,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and 34% <a href="/wiki/Lexical_similarity" title="Lexical similarity">lexically similar</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, Teochew has only 51% intelligibility with the Tong'an Hokkien|Tung'an dialect (Cheng 1997)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2019)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> whereas Mandarin and Amoy Min Nan are 62% phonetically similar<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and 15% lexically similar.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In comparison, German and English are 60% lexically similar.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hainanese" title="Hainanese">Hainanese</a>, which is sometimes considered Southern Min, has almost no mutual intelligibility with any form of Hokkien.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hokkien is an <a href="/wiki/Analytic_language" title="Analytic language">analytic language</a>; in a sentence, the arrangement of words is important to its meaning.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> A basic sentence follows the <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93verb%E2%80%93object" class="mw-redirect" title="Subject–verb–object">subject–verb–object</a> pattern (i.e. a <a href="/wiki/Subject_(grammar)" title="Subject (grammar)">subject</a> is followed by a <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">verb</a> then by an <a href="/wiki/Object_(grammar)" title="Object (grammar)">object</a>), though this order is often violated because Hokkien dialects are <a href="/wiki/Topic-prominent_language" title="Topic-prominent language">topic-prominent</a>. Unlike <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_language" title="Synthetic language">synthetic languages</a>, seldom do words indicate <a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">time</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plural" title="Plural">plural</a> by inflection. Instead, these concepts are expressed through adverbs, aspect markers, and grammatical particles, or are deduced from the context. Different particles are added to a <a href="/wiki/Sentence_(linguistics)" title="Sentence (linguistics)">sentence</a> to further specify its status or <a href="/wiki/Intonation_(linguistics)" title="Intonation (linguistics)">intonation</a>.
</p><p>A verb itself indicates no <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">grammatical tense</a>. The time can be explicitly shown with time-indicating adverbs. Certain exceptions exist, however, according to the pragmatic interpretation of a verb's meaning. Additionally, an optional <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">aspect</a> particle can be appended to a verb to indicate the state of an action. Appending interrogative or exclamative particles to a sentence turns a statement into a question or shows the attitudes of the speaker.
</p><p>Hokkien dialects preserve certain grammatical reflexes and patterns reminiscent of the broad stage of <a href="/wiki/Archaic_Chinese" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaic Chinese">Archaic Chinese</a>. This includes the <a href="/wiki/Serial_verb_construction" title="Serial verb construction">serialization of verb phrases</a> (direct linkage of verbs and <a href="/wiki/Verb_phrase" title="Verb phrase">verb phrases</a>) and the infrequency of <a href="/wiki/Nominalization" title="Nominalization">nominalization</a>, both similar to Archaic Chinese grammar.<sup id="cite_ref-McCoyLight1986_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCoyLight1986-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">汝</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">Lí</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="second person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">2SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">去</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">khì</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">go</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">買</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bué</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">buy</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">有</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">ū</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">have</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">錶仔</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">pió-á</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">watch</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">無？</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">--bô?</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">no</p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">汝</span> <span lang="zh">去</span> <span lang="zh">買</span> <span lang="zh">有</span> <span lang="zh">錶仔</span> <span lang="zh">無？</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">Lí</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">khì</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bué</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ū</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pió-á</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">--bô?</span></i></p><p style="display: none;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="second person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">2SG</abbr> go buy have watch no</p><p style="clear: left;">"Did you go to buy a watch?"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>Choice of grammatical function words also varies significantly among the Hokkien dialects. For instance, (<span lang="zh">乞</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">knit</span></i>) (denoting the causative, passive or dative) is retained in <a href="/wiki/Jinjiang,_Fujian" class="mw-redirect" title="Jinjiang, Fujian">Jinjiang</a> (also unique to the Jinjiang dialect is <span lang="zh">度</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">thō͘</span></i> and in <a href="/wiki/Jieyang" title="Jieyang">Jieyang</a>, but not in <a href="/wiki/Longxi_County,_Fujian" class="mw-redirect" title="Longxi County, Fujian">Longxi</a> and Xiamen, whose dialects use <span lang="zh">互／予</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">hō͘</span></i> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronouns">Pronouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Pronouns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hokkien dialects differ in the pronunciation of some pronouns (such as the second person pronoun <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lí</span></i>, <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lú</span></i>, or <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lír</span></i>), and also differ in how to form plural pronouns (such as <i><span lang="nan-Latn">n</span></i> or <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lâng</span></i>). Personal pronouns found in the Hokkien dialects are listed below:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">

<tbody><tr>
<th>
</th>
<th>Singular
</th>
<th>Plural
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>1st person
</th>
<td><span lang="zh">我</span><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">góa</span></i>
</td>
<td><span lang="zh">阮</span><sup>1</sup><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">gún, góan</span></i><br /><br /><span lang="zh">咱</span><sup>2</sup> or <span lang="zh">俺</span><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">lán</span></i> or <i><span lang="nan-Latn">án</span></i><br /><br /><span lang="zh">我儂</span><sup>1,3</sup><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">góa-lâng</span></i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>2nd person
</th>
<td><span lang="zh">汝</span><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">lí, lír, lú</span></i>
</td>
<td><span lang="zh">恁</span><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">lín</span></i><br /><br /><span lang="zh">汝儂</span><sup>3</sup><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">lí-lâng, lú-lâng</span></i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>3rd person
</th>
<td><span lang="zh">伊</span><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i>
</td>
<td><span lang="zh">𪜶</span><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">in</span></i><br /><br /><span lang="zh">伊儂</span><sup>3</sup><br /><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i-lâng</span></i>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<dl><dd><sup>1</sup> Exclusive</dd>
<dd><sup>2</sup> Inclusive</dd>
<dd><sup>3</sup> <span lang="zh">儂</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lâng</span></i> is typically suffixed in Southeast Asian Hokkien dialects (with the exception of Philippine Hokkien)</dd></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Possessive_pronoun" class="mw-redirect" title="Possessive pronoun">Possessive pronouns</a> can be marked by the particle <span lang="zh">的</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ê</span></i>), in the same way as normal nouns. In some dialects, possessive pronouns can also be formed with a nasal suffix, which means that possessive pronouns and plural pronouns are <a href="/wiki/Homophone" title="Homophone">homophones</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">阮</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">gún</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">翁</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">ang</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">姓</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">sìⁿ</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">陳。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">Tân</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">阮</span> <span lang="zh">翁</span> <span lang="zh">姓</span> <span lang="zh">陳。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">gún</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ang</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">sìⁿ</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">Tân</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"My husband's surname is <a href="/wiki/Chen_(surname)" title="Chen (surname)">Tan</a>."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The most common <a href="/wiki/Reflexive_pronoun" title="Reflexive pronoun">reflexive pronoun</a> is <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ka-kī</span></i> (<span lang="zh">家己</span>). In formal contexts, <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chū-kí</span></i> (<span lang="zh">自己</span>) is also used.
</p><p>Hokkien dialects use a variety of <a href="/wiki/Demonstrative_pronoun" class="mw-redirect" title="Demonstrative pronoun">demonstrative pronouns</a>, which include:
</p>
<ul><li>'this' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">che</span></i> (<span lang="zh">這</span>，<span lang="zh">即</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">chit-ê</span></i> (<span lang="zh">即個</span>)</li>
<li>'that' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">he</span></i> (<span lang="zh">許</span>，<span lang="zh">彼</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">hit-ê</span></i> (<span lang="zh">彼個</span>)</li>
<li>'here' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">hia</span></i> (<span lang="zh">遮</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">chit-tau</span></i> (<span lang="zh">即兜</span>)</li>
<li>'there' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">hia</span></i> (<span lang="zh">遐</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">hit-tau</span></i> (<span lang="zh">彼兜</span>)</li></ul>
<p>The interrogative pronouns include:
</p>
<ul><li>'what' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">siáⁿ-mih</span></i> (<span lang="zh">啥物</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">sím-mih</span></i> (<span lang="zh">甚麼</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">há-mi̍h</span></i> (<span lang="zh">何物</span>)</li>
<li>'when' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tī-sî</span></i> (<span lang="zh">底時</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">kúi-sî</span></i> (<span lang="zh">幾時</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">tang-sî</span></i> (<span lang="zh">當時</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">sím-mih sî-chūn</span></i> (<span lang="zh">甚麼時陣</span>)</li>
<li>'where' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tó-lo̍h</span></i> (<span lang="zh">倒落</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">tó-uī</span></i> (<span lang="zh">倒位</span>)</li>
<li>'who' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">siáⁿ-lâng</span></i> (<span lang="zh">啥人</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">siáng</span></i> (<span lang="zh">誰</span>),</li>
<li>'why' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ūi-siáⁿ-mih</span></i> (<span lang="zh">為啥物</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">ūi-sím-mih</span></i> (<span lang="zh">為甚物</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">án-chóaⁿ</span></i> (<span lang="zh">按怎</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">khah</span></i> (<span lang="zh">盍</span>)</li>
<li>'how' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">án-chóaⁿ</span></i> (<span lang="zh">按怎</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">lû-hô</span></i> (<span lang="zh">如何</span>)，<i><span lang="nan-Latn">cháiⁿ-iūⁿ</span></i> (<span lang="zh">怎樣</span>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Copula">Copula</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Copula"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>States and qualities are generally expressed using <a href="/wiki/Stative_verbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Stative verbs">stative verbs</a> that do not require a verb meaning 'to be':
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">我</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">goá</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">腹肚</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">pak-tó͘</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">stomach</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">枵。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">iau.</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">hungry</p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">我</span> <span lang="zh">腹肚</span> <span lang="zh">枵。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">goá</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pak-tó͘</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">iau.</span></i></p><p style="display: none;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr> stomach hungry</p><p style="clear: left;">"I am hungry."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>With noun complements, the verb <i><span lang="nan-Latn">sī</span></i> (<span lang="zh">是</span>) serves as the verb 'to be'.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">昨昏</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">cha-hng</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">是</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">sī</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">八月節。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">poeh-ge̍h-choeh.</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">昨昏</span> <span lang="zh">是</span> <span lang="zh">八月節。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">cha-hng</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">sī</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">poeh-ge̍h-choeh.</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"Yesterday was the Mid-Autumn festival."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>To indicate location, the words <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tī</span></i> (<span lang="zh">佇</span>) <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tiàm</span></i> (<span lang="zh">踮</span>), <i><span lang="nan-Latn">leh</span></i> (<span lang="zh">咧</span>), which are collectively known as the locatives or sometimes coverbs in Chinese linguistics, are used to express '(to be) at':
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">我</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">goá</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">踮</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">tiàm</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">遮</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">chia</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">等</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">tán</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">汝。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">lí.</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">我</span> <span lang="zh">踮</span> <span lang="zh">遮</span> <span lang="zh">等</span> <span lang="zh">汝。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">goá</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tiàm</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chia</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tán</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lí.</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"I am here waiting for you."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">伊</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">這摆</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">chit-mái</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">佇</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">tī</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">厝</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">chhù</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">裡</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">lāi</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">咧</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">leh</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">睏。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">khùn.</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">伊</span> <span lang="zh">這摆</span> <span lang="zh">佇</span> <span lang="zh">厝</span> <span lang="zh">裡</span> <span lang="zh">咧</span> <span lang="zh">睏。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chit-mái</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tī</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chhù</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lāi</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">leh</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">khùn.</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"They're sleeping at home now."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Negation">Negation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Negation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hokkien dialects have a variety of negation particles that are prefixed or affixed to the verbs they modify. There are six primary negation particles in Hokkien dialects (with some variation in how they are <a href="/wiki/Written_Hokkien#Chinese_characters" title="Written Hokkien">written in characters</a>):
</p>
<ol><li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">m̄</span></i> (<span lang="zh">毋</span>，<span lang="zh">呣</span>，<span lang="zh">唔</span>，<span lang="zh">伓</span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bē</span></i> (<span lang="zh">未</span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bōe</span></i> (<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Be-tw.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Be-tw.svg/15px-Be-tw.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Be-tw.svg/23px-Be-tw.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Be-tw.svg/30px-Be-tw.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a></span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">mài</span></i> (<span lang="zh">莫</span>，<span lang="zh">【勿愛】</span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i> (<span lang="zh">無</span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">put</span></i> (<span lang="zh">不</span>) – literary</li></ol>
<p>Other negative particles include:
</p>
<ol><li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bâng</span></i> (<span lang="zh">甭</span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bián</span></i> (<span lang="zh">免</span>)</li>
<li><i><span lang="nan-Latn">thài</span></i> (<span lang="zh">汰</span>)</li></ol>
<p>The particle <i><span lang="nan-Latn">m̄</span></i> (<span lang="zh">毋</span>，<span lang="zh">呣</span>，<span lang="zh">唔</span>，<span lang="zh">伓</span>) is general and can negate almost any verb:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">伊</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">毋</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">m̄</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">not</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">捌</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bat</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">know</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">字。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">jī</span></i></p><p style="margin: 0px;">character</p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">伊</span> <span lang="zh">毋</span> <span lang="zh">捌</span> <span lang="zh">字。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">m̄</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bat</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">jī</span></i></p><p style="display: none;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr> not know character</p><p style="clear: left;">"They cannot read."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The particle <i><span lang="nan-Latn">mài</span></i> (<span lang="zh">莫</span>，<span lang="zh">【勿爱】</span>), a concatenation of <i><span lang="nan-Latn">m-ài</span></i> (<span lang="zh">毋愛</span>) is used to negate imperative commands:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">莫</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">mài</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">講！</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">kóng</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">莫</span> <span lang="zh">講！</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">mài</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">kóng</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"Don't speak!"</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The particle <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i> (<span lang="zh">無</span>) indicates the past tense:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (October 2023)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Hokkien#Dubious" title="Talk:Hokkien">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">伊</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">無</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">食。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">chia̍h</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">伊</span> <span lang="zh">無</span> <span lang="zh">食。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chia̍h</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"They did not eat."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The verb 'to have', <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ū</span></i> (<span lang="zh">有</span>) is replaced by <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i> (<span lang="zh">無</span>) when negated (not <span lang="zh">無有</span>):
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">伊</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">無</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">錢。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">chîⁿ</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">伊</span> <span lang="zh">無</span> <span lang="zh">錢。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bô</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chîⁿ</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">"They do not have any money."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>The particle <i><span lang="nan-Latn">put</span></i> (<span lang="zh">不</span>) is used infrequently, mostly found in literary compounds and phrases:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">伊</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">真</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">chin</span></i></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><span lang="zh">不孝。</span></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">put-hàu</span></i></p></div><p style="display: none;"><span lang="zh">伊</span> <span lang="zh">真</span> <span lang="zh">不孝。</span></p><p style="display: none;"><i><span lang="nan-Latn">i</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chin</span></i> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">put-hàu</span></i></p><p style="clear: left;">They are really unfilial."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The majority of Hokkien vocabulary is <a href="/wiki/Monosyllabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Monosyllabic">monosyllabic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2016)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Many Hokkien <a href="/wiki/Word" title="Word">words</a> have <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognates</a> in other Chinese varieties. That said, there are also many indigenous words that are unique to Hokkien and are potentially not of <a href="/wiki/Sino-Tibetan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sino-Tibetan">Sino-Tibetan</a> origin, while others are shared by all the <a href="/wiki/Min_Chinese" title="Min Chinese">Min</a> dialects (e.g. 'congee' is <span lang="zh">糜</span> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">mê</span></i>, <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bôe</span></i>, <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bê</span></i>, not <span lang="zh">粥</span> <i><span lang="zh-Latn">zhōu</span></i>, as in other dialects).
</p><p>As compared to Mandarin, Hokkien dialects prefer to use the monosyllabic form of words, without suffixes. For instance, the Mandarin noun suffix <span lang="zh">子</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">zi</span></i>) is not found in Hokkien words, while another noun suffix, <span lang="zh">仔</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">á</span></i>) is used in many nouns. Examples are below:
</p>
<ul><li>'duck' – <span lang="zh">鴨</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ah</span></i> or <span lang="zh">鴨仔</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ah-á</span></i> (cf. Mandarin <span lang="zh">鴨子</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">yāzi</span></i>)</li>
<li>'color' – <span lang="zh">色</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">sek</span></i> (cf. Mandarin <span lang="zh">顏色</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">yán sè</span></i>)</li></ul>
<p>In other bisyllabic morphemes, the syllables are inverted, as compared to Mandarin. Examples include the following:
</p>
<ul><li>'guest' – <span lang="zh">人客</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">lâng-kheh</span></i> (cf. Mandarin <span lang="zh">客人</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">kèrén</span></i>)</li></ul>
<p>In other cases, the same word can have different meanings in Hokkien and Mandarin. Similarly, depending on the region Hokkien is spoken in, loanwords from local languages (Malay, Tagalog, Burmese, among others), as well as other Chinese dialects (such as Southern Chinese dialects like Cantonese and <a href="/wiki/Teochew_dialect" title="Teochew dialect">Teochew</a>), are commonly integrated into the vocabulary of Hokkien dialects.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_and_colloquial_readings">Literary and colloquial readings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Literary and colloquial readings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The existence of <a href="/wiki/Literary_and_colloquial_reading" class="mw-redirect" title="Literary and colloquial reading">literary and colloquial readings</a> is a prominent feature of some Hokkien dialects and indeed in many Sinitic varieties in the south. The bulk of literary readings (<span lang="zh">文讀</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bûn-tha̍k</span></i>), based on pronunciations of the vernacular during the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a>, are mainly used in formal phrases and written language (e.g. philosophical concepts, given names, and some place names), while the colloquial (or vernacular) ones (<span lang="zh">白讀</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pe̍h-tha̍k</span></i>) are usually used in spoken language, vulgar phrases and surnames. Literary readings are more similar to the pronunciations of the Tang standard of Middle Chinese than their colloquial equivalents. 
</p><p>The pronounced divergence between literary and colloquial pronunciations found in Hokkien dialects is attributed to the presence of several strata in the Min lexicon. The earliest, colloquial stratum is traced to the <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> (206 BCE – 220 CE); the second colloquial one comes from the period of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_and_Southern_dynasties" title="Northern and Southern dynasties">Northern and Southern dynasties</a> (420–589 CE); the third stratum of pronunciations (typically literary ones) comes from the Tang dynasty (618–907 CE) and is based on the <a href="/wiki/Prestige_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestige dialect">prestige dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang&#39;an">Chang'an</a> (modern day <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi&#39;an">Xi'an</a>), its capital.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some commonly seen sound correspondences (colloquial → literary) are as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>p- (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[p-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[pʰ-]</span>) → h (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[h-]</span>)</li>
<li>ch-, chh- (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ts-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tsʰ-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tɕ-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tɕʰ-]</span>) → s (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[s-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɕ-]</span>)</li>
<li>k-, kh- (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[k-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[kʰ-]</span>) → ch (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tɕ-]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tɕʰ-]</span>)</li>
<li>-ⁿ (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-ã]</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-uã]</span>) → n (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-an]</span>)</li>
<li>-h (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-ʔ]</span>) → t (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-t]</span>)</li>
<li>i (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-i]</span>) → e (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-e]</span>)</li>
<li>e (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-e]</span>) → a (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-a]</span>)</li>
<li>ia (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-ia]</span>) → i (<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[-i]</span>)</li></ul>
<p>This table displays some widely used characters in Hokkien that have both literary and colloquial readings:<sup id="cite_ref-mothertongue_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mothertongue-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MoE_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoE-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>

<p>This feature extends to <a href="/wiki/Chinese_numerals" title="Chinese numerals">Chinese numerals</a>, which have both literary and colloquial readings.<sup id="cite_ref-MoE_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoE-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Literary readings are typically used when the numerals are read out loud (e.g. phone numbers, years), while colloquial readings are used for counting items.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Semantic_differences_between_Hokkien_and_Mandarin">Semantic differences between Hokkien and Mandarin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Semantic differences between Hokkien and Mandarin"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Quite a few words from the variety of <a href="/wiki/Old_Chinese" title="Old Chinese">Old Chinese</a> spoken in the state of <a href="/wiki/Wu_(state)" title="Wu (state)">Wu</a>, where the ancestral language of Min and Wu dialect families originated, and later words from <a href="/wiki/Middle_Chinese" title="Middle Chinese">Middle Chinese</a> as well, have retained the original meanings in Hokkien, while many of their counterparts in <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a> have either fallen out of daily use, have been substituted with other words (some of which are borrowed from other languages while others are new developments), or have developed newer meanings. The same may be said of Hokkien as well, since some lexical meaning evolved in step with Mandarin while others are wholly innovative developments.
</p><p>This table shows some Hokkien dialect words from Classical Chinese, as contrasted to the written Mandarin:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Words_from_Min_Yue">Words from Min Yue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Words from Min Yue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some commonly used words, shared by all<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2016)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Hokkien#Dubious" title="Talk:Hokkien">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> Min Chinese languages, came from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Yue_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Yue languages">Old Yue languages</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Norman_(sinologist)" title="Jerry Norman (sinologist)">Jerry Norman</a> suggested that these languages were <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Austroasiatic">Austroasiatic</a>. Some terms are thought be cognates with words in <a href="/wiki/Tai_Kadai" class="mw-redirect" title="Tai Kadai">Tai Kadai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a> languages. They include the following examples, compared to the <a href="/wiki/Fuzhou_dialect" title="Fuzhou dialect">Fuzhou dialect</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Min_Dong_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Min Dong language">Min Dong language</a>:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loanwords">Loanwords</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hokkien&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Loanwords"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">Loanwords</a> are not unusual among Hokkien dialects, as speakers readily adopted indigenous terms of the languages they came in contact with. As a result, there is a plethora of loanwords that are not mutually comprehensible among Hokkien dialects.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwanese Hokkien</a>, as a result of linguistic contact with <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Formosan_languages" title="Formosan languages">Formosan languages</a>, contains many loanwords from these languages. Many words have also been formed as <a href="/wiki/Calque" title="Calque">calques</a> from Mandarin, and speakers will often directly use Mandarin vocabulary through <a href="/wiki/Codeswitching" class="mw-redirect" title="Codeswitching">codeswitching</a>. Among these include the following examples:
</p>
<ul><li>'toilet' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">piān-só͘</span></i> (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%BE%BF%E6%89%80" class="extiw" title="wikt:便所">便所</a></span></span>) from Japanese <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">benjo</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">便所</span></span>)</span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hant">屎礐</span></span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">sái-ha̍k</i></span>), <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hant">廁所</span></span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">chhek-só͘</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'car' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chū-tōng-chhia</span></i> (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%BB%8A" class="extiw" title="wikt:自動車">自動車</a></span></span>) from Japanese <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">jidōsha</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">自動車</span></span>)</span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%A2%A8" class="extiw" title="wikt:風">風</a>車</span></span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">hong-chhia</i></span>), <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hant">汽車</span></span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">khì-chhia</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'to admire' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">kám-sim</span></i> (<span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%84%9F%E5%BF%83" class="extiw" title="wikt:感心">感心</a></span>) from Japanese <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">kanshin</i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">感心</span></span>)</span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hant"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%84%9F%E5%8B%95" class="extiw" title="wikt:感動">感動</a></span></span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">kám-tōng</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'fruit' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chúi-ké / chúi-kóe / chúi-kér</span></i> (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%B0%B4%E6%9E%9C" class="extiw" title="wikt:水果">水果</a></span></span>) from Mandarin (<span lang="zh">水果</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">shuǐguǒ</span></i>)
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">果子</span></span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">ké-chí</i></span> / <span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">kóe-chí</i></span> / <span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">kér-chí</i></span>)</dd></dl></li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Singaporean_Hokkien" title="Singaporean Hokkien">Singaporean Hokkien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penang_Hokkien" title="Penang Hokkien">Penang Hokkien</a> and other Malaysian Hokkien dialects tend to draw loanwords from <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as well as other Chinese dialects, primarily <a href="/wiki/Teochew_dialect" title="Teochew dialect">Teochew</a>. Examples include:
</p>
<ul><li>'but' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ta-pi</span></i>, from Malay
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">但是</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">tān-sī</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'doctor' – <span lang="zh">老君</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ló-kun</span></i>, from Malay <span title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text"><i lang="ms">dukun</i></span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">醫生</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">i-seng</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'stone', 'rock' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bà-tû</span></i>, from Malay <span title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text"><i lang="ms">batu</i></span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">石头</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">chio̍h-thâu</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'market' – <span lang="zh">巴剎</span> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pa-sat</span></i>, from Malay <span title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text"><i lang="ms">pasar</i></span> from Persian <span title="Persian-language romanization"><i lang="fa-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a></i></span> (<span title="Persian-language text"><span lang="fa" dir="rtl">بازار</span></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-似懂非懂2006_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-似懂非懂2006-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">市場</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">chhī-tiûⁿ</i></span>), <span lang="zh">菜市</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">chhài-chhī</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'they' – <span lang="zh">伊儂</span> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">i-lâng</span></i> from Teochew (<span title="Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="zh-Latn">i1 nang5</i></span>)
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">c𪜶</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">in</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'together' – <span lang="zh">做瓠</span> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chò-bú</span></i> from Teochew <span lang="zh">做瓠</span> (<span title="Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="zh-Latn">jo3 bu5</i></span>)
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">做夥</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">chò-hóe</i></span>), <span lang="zh">同齊</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">tâng-chê</i></span>) or <span lang="zh">鬥陣</span> (<span title="Min Nan Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="nan-Latn">tàu-tīn</i></span>)</dd></dl></li>
<li>'soap' – <span lang="zh">雪文</span> <i><span lang="nan-Latn">sap-bûn</span></i> from Malay <span title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text"><i lang="ms">sabun</i></span>, from Arabic <span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">ṣābūn</i></span> (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar" dir="rtl">صابون</span></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-似懂非懂2006_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-似懂非懂2006-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Watters1889_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watters1889-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Philippine Hokkien, as a result of centuries-old contact with both Philippine languages and Spanish also incorporate words from these languages. Speakers today will also often directly use <a href="/wiki/Philippine_English" title="Philippine English">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>), or other <a href="/wiki/Philippine_languages" title="Philippine languages">Philippine languages</a> like <a href="/wiki/Cebuano_language" title="Cebuano language">Bisaya</a>, vocabulary through <a href="/wiki/Codeswitching" class="mw-redirect" title="Codeswitching">codeswitching</a>. Examples include:
</p>
<ul><li>'cup' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ba-sù</span></i>, from either <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> <span title="Tagalog-language text"><i lang="tl">baso</i></span> or Spanish <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">vaso</i></span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">杯仔</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">poe-á</span></i>, <span lang="zh">杯</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">poe</span></i></dd></dl></li>
<li>'office' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">o-pi-sín</span></i>, from Tagalog <span title="Tagalog-language text"><i lang="tl">opisina</i></span>, which itself is from Spanish <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">oficina</i></span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">辦公室</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pān-kong-sek/pān-kong-siak</span></i></dd></dl></li>
<li>'soap' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">sap-bûn</span></i>, from either Tagalog <span title="Tagalog-language text"><i lang="tl">sabon</i></span> or <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_Spanish" title="Early Modern Spanish">Early Modern Spanish</a> <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">xabon</i></span></li>
<li>'coffee' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ka-pé</span></i>, from Tagalog <span title="Tagalog-language text"><i lang="tl">kape</i></span>, which itself is from Spanish <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">café</i></span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">咖啡</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ko-pi</span></i>, <span lang="zh">咖啡</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">ka-pi</span></i></dd></dl></li>
<li>'to pay' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pá-lâ</span></i>, from Spanish <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">pagar</i></span>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">予錢</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">hō͘-chîⁿ</span></i>, <span lang="zh">還錢</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">hêng-chîⁿ</span></i></dd></dl></li>
<li>'dozen' – <i><span lang="nan-Latn">lo-sin</span></i>, from <a href="/wiki/Philippine_English" title="Philippine English">Philippine English</a> <i>dozen</i>
<dl><dd>Other Hokkien variants: <span lang="zh">打</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">táⁿ</span></i></dd></dl></li></ul>
<p>Philippine Hokkien usually follows the 3 decimal place <a href="/wiki/Hindu%E2%80%93Arabic_numeral_system" title="Hindu–Arabic numeral system">Hindu-Arabic numeral system</a> used worldwide, but still retains the concept of <span lang="zh">萬</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bān</span></i>; &#39;ten thousand&#39; from the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_numerals" title="Chinese numerals">Chinese numeral system</a>, so 'ten thousand' would be <span lang="zh">一萬</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chi̍t-bān</span></i>, but 'eleven thousand' would be <span lang="zh">十一千</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">cha̍p-it-chheng</span></i> instead of <span lang="zh">一萬一千</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chi̍t-bān chi̍t-chheng</span></i>, and so on. Philippine Hokkien additionally has words for 'million': <span lang="zh">桶</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">tháng</span></i> or <span lang="zh">面桶</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">bīn-tháng</span></i>, instead of <span lang="zh">百萬</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">pah-bān</span></i>, so 'one million' would be <span lang="zh">一桶</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chi̍t-tháng</span></i> or <span lang="zh">一面桶</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chi̍t-bīn-tháng</span></i>; sometimes 'one hundred million' would be <span lang="zh">一百桶</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chi̍t-pah-tháng</span></i> or <span lang="zh">一億</span>; <i><span lang="nan-Latn">chi̍t-iak</span></i>.
</p>
